     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Rivalries_3">
       Rivalries
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Southeastern_Conference&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Rivalries">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Tennessee_Lady_Volunteers_basketball" title="Tennessee Lady Volunteers basketball">
        Tennessee
       </a>
       -
       <a href="/wiki/Connecticut_Huskies_women%27s_basketball" title="Connecticut Huskies women's basketball">
        UConn
       </a>
      </li>
     </ul>
     <div class="hatnote">
      See also:
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tennessee-UConn_rivalry" title="Tennessee-UConn rivalry">
       Tennessee-UConn rivalry
      </a>
     </div>
     <dl>
      <dd>
       The Lady Vols have historically been one of the nation's dominant programs in that sport. Starting in the mid-1990s, UConn has emerged as Tennessee's main rival for national prominence. The Huskies won four national titles between 2000 and 2004; in three of those years, their opponent in the NCAA final was Tennessee. Connecticut also defeated Tennessee in the 1995 Championship game, the Huskies' first-ever title.
      </dd>
     </dl>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Other_sports">
       Other sports
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Southeastern_Conference&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Other sports">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      Besides football, basketball, and baseball, there are a number of other sports in which the Southeastern Conference actively competes.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Rivalries_4">
       Rivalries
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Southeastern_Conference&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Rivalries">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Alabama_Crimson_Tide_women%27s_gymnastics" title="Alabama Crimson Tide women's gymnastics">
        Alabama
       </a>
       -
       <a href="/wiki/Georgia_Gym_Dogs" title="Georgia Gym Dogs">
        Georgia
       </a>
       , women's gymnastics
      </li>
     </ul>
     <dl>
      <dd>
       These two storied programs have often butted heads for not only SEC titles, but NCAA titles, as well. Georgia has won ten national championships to Alabama's six. For decades the rivalry was dominated by the two long standing coaches of the two schools,
       <a href="/wiki/Suzanne_Yoculan" title="Suzanne Yoculan">
        Suzanne Yoculan
       </a>
       of Georgia and
       <a href="/wiki/Sarah_Patterson_(coach)" title="Sarah Patterson (coach)">
        Sarah Patterson
       </a>
       of Alabama. Yoculan and Patterson have since retired, bringing their personal rivalry to an end.
      </dd>
     </dl>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/University_of_Alabama_athletics" title="University of Alabama athletics">
        Alabama
       </a>
       -
       <a href="/wiki/University_of_Florida" title="University of Florida">
        Florida
       </a>
       , women's softball
      </li>
     </ul>
     <dl>
      <dd>
       These two nationally acclaimed softball programs have proven to be the elite of the SEC and the nation. While consistently being ranked in the nation's Top Ten, both teams find their way to the SEC Tournament Finals and often clash once more in the Women's College Softball World Series.
      </dd>
     </dl>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Auburn_Tigers_swimming_and_diving" title="Auburn Tigers swimming and diving">
        Auburn
       </a>
       -
       <a href="/wiki/Texas_Longhorns" title="Texas Longhorns">
        Texas
       </a>
       , men's swimming and diving
      </li>
     </ul>
     <dl>
      <dd>
       One of the youngest rivalries featuring an SEC team, the Tigers and Texas Longhorns are the two most successful swimming and diving programs in the country. The two have combined for 17 NCAA National Titles since 1981 (9 for Texas, 8 for Auburn) and between 1999 and 2007 won every national title awarded. The two regularly face off in a meet during the regular season, Auburn's men own an 129 record over the Longhorns. The women just recently began an annual series, with the Tigers winning the series so far 31. Texas was the only team to beat the Auburn men between 2001 and 2007.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Texas_62-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Texas-62">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         59
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       Kentucky Louisville men's college basketball
      </dd>
     </dl>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="National_team_championships">
       National team championships
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Southeastern_Conference&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: National team championships">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_SEC_national_champions" title="List of SEC national champions">
       List of SEC national champions
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Since the SEC's founding in December 1932, the varsity athletic teams of its current 14 members have won over 200 national team sports championships.
     </p>
     <p>
      The following is the list of the national team championships claimed by current SEC member schools, including those tournament championships currently or formerly sponsored by the
      <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">
       National Collegiate Athletic Association
      </a>
      (NCAA).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ncaa_mens_titles_63-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-ncaa_mens_titles-63">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        60
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ncaa_womens_titles_64-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-ncaa_womens_titles-64">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        61
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The NCAA has never sponsored a tournament championship for major college football, the championship game for which is currently part of the
      <a href="/wiki/College_Football_Playoff" title="College Football Playoff">
       College Football Playoff
      </a>
      (CFP) system. Prior to 1992, championships for major college football were determined by a "consensus" of major polling services, including the
      <a href="/wiki/AP_Poll" title="AP Poll">
       Associated Press
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/United_Press_International" title="United Press International">
       United Press International
      </a>
      college football polls. Recognized
      <a href="/wiki/Association_for_Intercollegiate_Athletics_for_Women_championships" title="Association for Intercollegiate Athletics for Women championships">
       women's championships
      </a>
      from 1972 to 1982 were administered by the
      <a href="/wiki/Association_for_Intercollegiate_Athletics_for_Women" title="Association for Intercollegiate Athletics for Women">
       Association for Intercollegiate Athletics for Women
      </a>
      (AIAW), not the NCAA. There was a one-year overlap period during the 198182 school year, when both the AIAW and the NCAA operated women's championship tournaments; since 1982, only the NCAA has sponsored women's championship tournaments. National equestrian tournament championships are currently sponsored by the
      <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Equestrian_Association" title="National Collegiate Equestrian Association">
       National Collegiate Equestrian Association
      </a>
      (NCEA), not the NCAA. Those national championships dating from before 1933 predate the founding of the SEC in December 1932; championships won by Arkansas and South Carolina before the 199293 school year predate their membership in the SEC; championships won by Missouri and Texas A&amp;M before the 201213 school year predate their membership in the SEC.
     </p>

           </b>

     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="National_team_titles_claimed_by_current_SEC_institutions">
       National team titles claimed by current SEC institutions
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Southeastern_Conference&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: National team titles claimed by current SEC institutions">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      The fourteen members of the Southeastern Conference claim over 200 national team championships in sports currently or formerly sponsored by conference members. The following totals include national team championships sponsored by the
      <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">
       National Collegiate Athletic Association
      </a>
      (NCAA) from 1906 to the present, the
      <a href="/wiki/Association_for_Intercollegiate_Athletics_for_Women" title="Association for Intercollegiate Athletics for Women">
       Association for Intercollegiate Athletics for Women
      </a>
      (AIAW) from 1972 to 1982, and, in football, the
      <a href="/wiki/Bowl_Alliance" title="Bowl Alliance">
       Bowl Alliance
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Bowl_Coalition" title="Bowl Coalition">
       Bowl Coalition
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Bowl_Championship_Series" title="Bowl Championship Series">
       Bowl Championship Series
      </a>
      (BCS) and
      <a href="/wiki/College_Football_Playoff" title="College Football Playoff">
       College Football Playoff
      </a>
      (CFP) since 1992, as well as consensus national championships determined by the major football polls prior to 1992.
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       LSU  46
      </li>
      <li>
       Arkansas  43
      </li>
      <li>
       Georgia  36
      </li>
      <li>
       Florida  35
      </li>
      <li>
       Alabama  25
      </li>
      <li>
       Tennessee  23
      </li>
      <li>
       Auburn  19
      </li>
      <li>
       Texas A&amp;M  17
      </li>
      <li>
       Kentucky  11
      </li>
      <li>
       South Carolina  9
      </li>
      <li>
       Mississippi  3
      </li>
      <li>
       Vanderbilt  3
      </li>
      <li>
       Missouri  2
      </li>
      <li>
       Mississippi State  0
      </li>
     </ul>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="NCAA_and_AIAW_national_tournament_team_titles_won_by_current_SEC_institutions">
       NCAA and AIAW national tournament team titles won by current SEC institutions
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Southeastern_Conference&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: NCAA and AIAW national tournament team titles won by current SEC institutions">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      The following totals include national team tournament championships sponsored by the
      <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">
       National Collegiate Athletic Association
      </a>
      (NCAA) from 1906 to the present and the
      <a href="/wiki/Association_for_Intercollegiate_Athletics_for_Women" title="Association for Intercollegiate Athletics for Women">
       Association for Intercollegiate Athletics for Women
      </a>
      (AIAW) from 1972 to 1982. The NCAA did not sponsor tournament championships in women's sports before the 198182 academic year, and the NCAA has never sponsored a national championship playoff or tournament in major college football. To date, the fourteen members of the SEC have won 212 NCAA and four AIAW championships,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">
       <a href="#cite_note-65">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        62
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      including:
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       LSU  43
      </li>
      <li>
       Arkansas  42
      </li>
      <li>
       Florida  32
      </li>
      <li>
       Georgia  28
      </li>
      <li>
       Tennessee  17
      </li>
      <li>
       Auburn  14
      </li>
      <li>
       Texas A&amp;M  12
      </li>
      <li>
       Kentucky  10
      </li>
      <li>
       Alabama  10
      </li>
      <li>
       South Carolina  3
      </li>
      <li>
       Vanderbilt  3
      </li>
      <li>
       Missouri  2
      </li>
      <li>
       Mississippi  0
      </li>
      <li>
       Mississippi State  0
      </li>
     </ul>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Television_and_radio_contracts">
       Television and radio contracts
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Southeastern_Conference&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Television and radio contracts">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      The SEC televises football games across various networks during the fall. SEC coverage is primarily provided by
      <a href="/wiki/CBS" title="CBS">
       CBS
      </a>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/ESPN" title="ESPN">
       ESPN
      </a>
      family of networks, which includes ESPN,
      <a href="/wiki/ESPN2" title="ESPN2">
       ESPN2
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/ESPNU" title="ESPNU">
       ESPNU
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/ESPN_on_ABC" title="ESPN on ABC">
       ABC
      </a>
      .
      <a href="/wiki/Fox_Sports_Networks" title="Fox Sports Networks">
       Fox Sports Networks
      </a>
      also has rights to air seven live football games over the course of the season.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">
       <a href="#cite_note-66">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        63
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      ESPN reported paying $2.25 billion for broadcast rights of SEC football games beginning in the 2009 season and running through fiscal year 2025.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">
       <a href="#cite_note-67">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        64
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Games scheduled for airing are generally picked two weeks before they occur, with a few matches that are selected by CBS and ESPN prior to the season.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2013)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      CBS has the first pick for a game and selects the highest-profile game to broadcast to a national, over-the-air audience. The CBS game is usually broadcast at 3:30 Eastern. Some weekends, CBS will air a doubleheader of SEC games.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">
       <a href="#cite_note-68">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        65
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      CBS also has the rights for the SEC Championship Game.
     </p>
     <p>
      ESPN will air several SEC games each week among its various channels, with Saturday time slots generally at 12:00 ET, 7:00 ET, and 7:45 ET, and some SEC games will be shown on Thursday nights. In previous years,
      <a href="/wiki/Raycom_Sports" title="Raycom Sports">
       Raycom Sports
      </a>
      (and before it, Jefferson-Pilot/Lincoln Financial Sports) syndicated regional coverage for an SEC game of the week at 12:30 ET, but the new contract replaced it with a new ESPN-produced syndication package, the
      <a href="/wiki/SEC_Network" title="SEC Network">
       SEC Network
      </a>
      whose football games kickoff at 12:21 ET.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">
       <a href="#cite_note-69">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        66
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The currently scheduled Fox Sports Net games are set for 7:00 ET.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-secsports.com_70-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-secsports.com-70">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        67
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      For games not selected by any broadcast provider, certain schools may offer regional pay-per-view.
     </p>
     <p>
      As of 2008, all SEC schools are affiliated with XM Radio, offering their radio broadcasts to an audience on XM. According to SiriusXM, the SEC will not be included as part of the "Best of XM" package deal for Sirius customers.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="2008_television_contract">
       2008 television contract
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Southeastern_Conference&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: 2008 television contract">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      During the 20072008 fiscal year review meeting, there was discussion among SEC leadership about the possibility of starting a TV network dedicated to its conference, much in the same way the
      <a href="/wiki/Mountain_West_Conference" title="Mountain West Conference">
       Mountain West Conference
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Big_Ten_Conference" title="Big Ten Conference">
       Big Ten Conference
      </a>
      have done with
      <a href="/wiki/MountainWest_Sports_Network" title="MountainWest Sports Network">
       the mtn.
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Big_Ten_Network" title="Big Ten Network">
       Big Ten Networks
      </a>
      , respectively. A decision was made to postpone the decision until at least the following year.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">
       <a href="#cite_note-71">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        68
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In August 2008, the SEC announced an unprecedented 15-year television contract with CBS worth an estimated $55 million a year. This continues the relationship the SEC already has with CBS, which puts the SEC in the unique position as the only conference to have its own exclusive national television network of the four major over-the-air broadcast networks (CBS, NBC, ABC, Fox) to display the SEC's events.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-about_10-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-about-10">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        7
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In the same month, the league also announced another landmark television contract with ESPN worth $2.25 billion or $150 million a year for the life of the contract, which is for fifteen years. It is the longest and wealthiest contract among all television deals among the major conferences. With these contracts, the SEC had, at the time of the deal, the richest television deals in the country outside the Big Ten and helped make the SEC one of the most nationally televised and visible conferences in the country with the coverage that was provided by these contracts.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">
       <a href="#cite_note-72">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        69
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">
       <a href="#cite_note-73">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        70
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="2014_SEC_Network_Launch">
       2014 SEC Network Launch
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Southeastern_Conference&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: 2014 SEC Network Launch">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/SEC_Network" title="SEC Network">
       SEC Network
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/SEC_Network" title="SEC Network">
       SEC Network
      </a>
      is a
      <a href="/wiki/Television" title="Television">
       television
      </a>
      and multimedia network that features exclusively Southeastern Conference content through a partnership between
      <a href="/wiki/ESPN" title="ESPN">
       ESPN
      </a>
      and the SEC.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">
       <a href="#cite_note-74">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        71
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The network launched on August 14, 2014 with the first live football game scheduled for two weeks later between Texas A&amp;M and South Carolina on Thursday, August 28 in Columbia, S.C.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">
       <a href="#cite_note-75">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        72
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The network is part of a deal between the Southeastern Conference and ESPN which is a 20-year agreement, beginning in August 2014 and running through 2034. The agreement served to create and operate a new multiplatform television network and accompanying digital platform in the hope of increasing revenue for member institutions and expanding the reach of the Southeastern Conference.
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Conference_champions">
       Conference champions
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Southeastern_Conference&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Conference champions">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_Southeastern_Conference_champions" title="List of Southeastern Conference champions">
       List of Southeastern Conference champions
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      The
      <i>
       Southeastern Conference
      </i>
      sponsors nine men's sports and twelve women's sports, and awards a
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_Southeastern_Conference_champions" title="List of Southeastern Conference champions">
       conference championship
      </a>
      in every one of them.
     </p>

         </b>
        </span>
        M.Played in
        <a href="/wiki/Jacksonville,_Florida" title="Jacksonville, Florida">
         Jacksonville, Florida
        </a>
        . The rotates every year depending on which team is the designated home team. Also known as the "World's Largest Outdoor Cocktail Party" though use of the term is discouraged due to the issue of underage alcohol use.
       </li>
       <li>
        <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_n">
         <b>
          <a href="#ref_n">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        N.For decades the trophy of this game was a red, white, and blue
        <a href="/wiki/Bourbon_whiskey" title="Bourbon whiskey">
         bourbon
        </a>
        barrel, but this practice was discontinued in 1999 following a DUI accident that killed two Kentucky football players.
       </li>
       <li>
        <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_o">
         <b>
          <a href="#ref_o">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        O.Whereabouts of the original rag are unknown; a new rag was presented to LSU after victories in 2001 and 2006. Series was only contested twice from 1995 through 2005, but a 10-year contract began in 2006.
       </li>
       <li>
        <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_p">
         <b>
          <a href="#ref_p">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        P.Since joining the SEC this game has been played on or around Halloween every year, accordingly many students dress in costume for this game. The contrasting team colors are also typical Halloween colors.
       </li>
       <li>
        <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_q">
         <b>
          <a href="#ref_q">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        Q.For 74years the trophy of this game was the Beer Barrel: an orange, white, and blue beer keg. However, this practice was discontinued in 1999 following the aforementioned DUI accident.
       </li>
      </ul>
     </div>

          Megargee, Steve (June 26, 2015).
          <a class="external text" href="http://sports.yahoo.com/news/tennessee-set-move-lone-lady-vols-team-063654452--spt.html" rel="nofollow">
           "Tennessee set to make move to a lone 'Lady Vols' team"
          </a>
          .
          <a href="/wiki/Yahoo!_Sports" title="Yahoo! Sports">
           Yahoo! Sports
          </a>
          .
          <a href="/wiki/Associated_Press" title="Associated Press">

           <span class="nowrap">

           </span>
           2015
          </span>

          <q>
           An Associated Press survey of all 65 schools from the
           <a href="/wiki/Power_Five_conferences" title="Power Five conferences">
            five major conferences
           </a>
           found that at least 28 had separate nicknames for men's and women's teams at some point in their histories. Only seven continue that practice, and in most cases they only have separate nicknames for certain women's teams.
           <a href="/wiki/Texas_Tech_Red_Raiders_and_Lady_Raiders" title="Texas Tech Red Raiders and Lady Raiders">
            Texas Tech
           </a>
           uses the Lady Raiders for women's teams in sports that also have men's teams: basketball, tennis, golf, track and cross country. LSU uses a similar strategy.
          </q>

       <li id="cite_note-31">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-31">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         Under NCAA Bylaw 20.9.4, all Division I schools are required to sponsor a minimum of seven men's and seven women's sports, or six men's and eight women's sports. Bylaw 20.9.7.1 imposes the latter requirement on FBS schools. FCS schools, under Bylaw 20.9.8.1, may use either requirement. Note that this does not explicitly require that a school sponsor two more women's sports than men's sports. See
         <span class="citation web">
          <a class="external text" href="http://ncaapublications.com/productdownloads/D113.pdf" rel="nofollow">
           "201213 NCAA Division I Manual"
          </a>
          <span style="font-size:85%;">
           (PDF)
          </span>
          . NCAA
          <span class="reference-accessdate">
           . Retrieved
           <span class="nowrap">
            January 7,
           </span>
           2013
          </span>
          .
         </span>
         <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASoutheastern+Conference&amp;rft.btitle=2012%E2%80%9313+NCAA+Division+I+Manual&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fncaapublications.com%2Fproductdownloads%2FD113.pdf&amp;rft.pub=NCAA&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook">
          <span style="display:none;">
          </span>
         </span>
        </span>
